How Diversity of Animal Eyes Refutes Naturalism
Sanusi refutes natural causality via animal eye diversity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the diversity of animal eyes to refute natural causality and affirm that vision is directly created by Allah.

Core Idea
Vision is not from nature or anatomy—it is directly from Allah.

Sanusi presents a powerful empirical argument against those who attribute natural phenomena to inherent dispositions or physical causes. By pointing to the striking diversity in how different animals see—cats in darkness, pack animals by night and day—he shows that vision cannot be produced by the eye's anatomy alone. This lesson unpacks that argument and its theological conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the flow of Sanusi's argument. Note the key examples and the concluding praise.
Observe how the passage moves from examples to a general negation of natural causes.
2
Identify the refuted positions
Sanusi lists several false explanations for vision: nature, cause, emission of rays, eye anatomy (seven layers, brain connection). Underline each one in the translation.
These are the views of the naturalists (al-qāʾilūn bi-l-ṭabāʾiʿ wa-l-ʿilal).
3
Analyze the animal examples
Consider the cat (sees in darkness and daylight) and the pack animals (horses, mules, etc.). How does each example undermine a purely natural explanation?
Cats have a different visual need than humans, yet both see—showing vision adapts by divine choice, not fixed nature.
4
Grasp the theological conclusion
Sanusi concludes that any prevention of vision (e.g., darkness hindering human vision) occurs by Allah's pure choice, not by the physical conditions themselves. Vision itself is directly from Allah.
The verse 'So blessed is Allah, the best of creators' reinforces that creation is His direct act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنَّ مولانا سبحانه خالف بين أعين الحيوانات على قدر الحاجة إليها وتمام الانتفاع بها ، وليزول بذلك أوهام القائلين بالطبائع والعللِ ؛ فجعلَ تعالى الهرَّةَ تبصرُ في الظلام والنهار لتكمل بذلك منفعتها التي اختار سبحانه وتعالى أن يخلقها معها ، وكذا الكلابُ والبغال والخيلُ والحمير والجمالُ ؛ حتى يتمكَّنَ الإِنسانُ مِنَ السفرِ بها ليلاً ونهاراً ، وليعلمَ المُوفَّقُ أَنَّ رؤية الرائي ليسَتْ حاصلةً عن طبْعِ ولا علة، وليسَتْ بانبعاث أشعَةٍ مِنَ العين ، ولا مشروطاً فيها خصوص حاسة العين ، ولا طبقاتها السبع ، ولا استمدادها بما تستمدُّ به مِنَ الدماغ، ولا يمنعُ منها قُرْب ولا بُعْد، ولا حجاب مِنْ ظلمة أو غيرها، وما اتفقَ أَنْ يُوجَدَ معَ تلك الأمورِ مِنَ المنع فإنَّما هو بمخض اختيار الله تعالى أنْ يُوجد ذلك عندَها لا بها ، فتبارك الله أحسنُ الخالقين .
Then our Lord, glorified, made the eyes of animals differ according to the need for them and complete benefit from them, and so that the illusions of those who assert natural dispositions and causes might be removed. So He, exalted, made the cat see in darkness and daylight to complete thereby its benefit which He, glorified and exalted, chose to create with it. Likewise dogs, mules, horses, donkeys, and camels, so that man may travel with them by night and day, and so that the one granted success may know that the seeing of the seer is not produced by nature nor cause, nor is it by the emission of rays from the eye, nor is it conditioned upon the specific sense of the eye, nor its seven layers, nor its derivation from what it derives from the brain, nor does distance or proximity prevent it, nor a veil of darkness or anything else. And whatever prevention is found to occur alongside those things, it is only by the pure choice of Allah that He causes that to occur alongside them, not by them. So blessed is Allah, the best of creators.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage refutes naturalism (al-qāʾilūn bi-l-ṭabāʾiʿ wa-l-ʿilal) by citing diversity in animal eyes. God made animals see differently according to their needs: cats see in darkness and daylight, and beasts of burden see both night and day for human travel. This disproves that vision is produced by nature, cause, emission of rays, or the eye's specific anatomy (seven layers, brain connection). Vision is directly from God; any hindrance (e.g., darkness affecting vision) is merely concurrent by God's choice, not caused by those factors. The concluding praise affirms God as the best of creators, underscoring His direct action.

Key Terms
طبائع
علل
رؤية
انبعاث أشعة
اختيار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think vision depends solely on eye anatomy (e.g., seven layers, brain connection) and physical conditions (light, distance).
Correction: Sanusi shows that animal eye diversity—cats seeing in darkness, pack animals seeing day and night—proves vision is not limited by anatomy. Any hindrance (e.g., darkness preventing human vision) occurs by Allah's choice, not by the physical conditions themselves.

Checkpoint

B) The seven layers of the eye.
C) A connection to the brain.

Key Takeaway
The diversity of animal eyes proves that vision is not produced by nature, causes, or eye anatomy, but is directly created by Allah according to His wise choice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Refuting the Analogy of Human Cooperation
Sanusi refutes the analogy from human mutual lifting as evidence for two gods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the analogy of two humans lifting an object does not support the possibility of two gods cooperating, according to Sanusi's refutation based on the nature of created power and divine transcendence.

Core Idea
Human cooperation is not a valid analogy for divine cooperation because created power has no real effect.

In this passage, Sanusi takes up an objection that uses everyday human experience to argue for the possibility of multiple gods. The objector says: if two people can lift a heavy object together, why can't two gods cooperate in creation? Sanusi's response is sharp and decisive—he will show that the analogy itself is built on a false assumption about human power. By the end, you will see how the argument from human cooperation collapses when we properly understand causality and divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation once to get the flow of the argument. Don't analyze yet—just absorb the sequence.
2
Identify the objection and Sanusi's two-fold refutation
First, notice the objector's claim: two humans can lift a heavy object together, so two gods could cooperate. Then, see how Sanusi responds: first, he rejects the premise that lifting is an effect of created power; second, he shows that even if we grant that, the two lifters affect different parts of the object.
3
Connect to the broader theological principle
Reflect on why Sanusi insists that only Allah has true effect in bringing things into existence. How does this preserve the Islamic doctrine of tawhid (divine unity)?
This passage guards against any suggestion of partners in divinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما استشهدَ بهِ في تقرير هذا الاحتمالِ مِنْ أَنَّ الواحدَ منَّا لا يقدرُ على رفع شيء وحدَهُ ، فإذا انضم إليه غيرُه رفعاهُ : فبناءً على أنَّ الرفعَ أثر لقدرتنا الحادثة ، وذلك باطل عقلاً ونقلا (۱) ، وهذا الدليل الذي ذكرناه لإبطال هذا الاحتمالِ الذي قدَّرَهُ السائل .. متناوِلُ لإبطال ما استشهدَ بهِ أيضاً (۱) إذ الرافع له هو الرافع والخافض سبحانه وتعالى ، وليس لقدرتهما أثر الوجود ، هذا هو التحقيق ، وإن توهّمنا وجود مدخلية لقدرتهما في الإيجاد والتأثير .. فالجواب : ما رفعه الأول هو بعض هذا الشيء ، والثاني البعض الآخر ، وبه يُعلم استحالة اجتماع مؤثرين على أثر واحد حتى في الشاهد
As for what he cited in establishing this possibility — that one of us cannot lift something alone, but when another joins him, they lift it — it is based on the assumption that lifting is an effect of our created power, and that is invalid both rationally and by revelation. And this proof that we have mentioned for refuting this possibility that the questioner supposed... also covers refuting what he cited as evidence. (1) For the lifter is the One who raises and lowers (Allah), exalted and high, and there is no effect of their powers in existence. This is the verification. And if we were to imagine that their powers have an entry in bringing about and influencing... then the answer is: What the first one lifted is a part of this thing, and the second lifted the other part. And by this it is known the impossibility of two agents having effect on a single effect even in the witnessed realm.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. The objector gave the example of two humans lifting an object together to argue that two gods could cooperate. Sanusi responds that this analogy is false because the effect (lifting) in humans is an effect of our created power, and attributing effect to created power is false both rationally and by revelation. In reality, only Allah brings about existence; human power has no effect in bringing things into existence. If we suppose they have some role, then the first lifts part of the object and the second lifts the other part, so the effect is not one but two partial effects. Hence, the analogy fails even in the witnessed realm.

Key Terms
رفع (lifting)
قدرة حادثة (created power)
أثر (effect)
مؤثرين (agents of effect)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human cooperation (e.g., two people lifting a heavy object) is a valid analogy to argue that two gods could cooperate in creation.
Correction: Sanusi shows that human power does not actually produce any effect in bringing things into existence; it is Allah who is the true cause. Even if humans have some role, they affect distinct parts, not a single effect. Therefore, the analogy does not apply to divine action.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is the analogy of two humans lifting an object invalid for proving two gods?
A) Because human power is created and has no real effect on bringing things into existence
B) Because two humans cannot lift the same object at the same time
C) Because the object is actually lifted by Allah through the humans
D) Because the example is not mentioned in the Quran

Key Takeaway
Sanusi refutes the analogy of human cooperation by asserting that created power has no effect in bringing things into existence, and even if it did, each agent affects a distinct part, so two agents cannot produce one single effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though your efforts have no effect except by Allah’s will, or do you secretly rely on your own power? In what specific situation today will you remind yourself that the outcome is entirely from Him?
?
When you see others cooperating to achieve something, does your heart ever feel that their combined strength produced the result? How can you train your mind to see that every part—each partial effect—is decreed by Allah alone?
?
If Sanusi is right that no two agents can produce a single effect, then only Allah can create, sustain, and guide your soul. Are you willing to abandon every false sense of shared control and surrender completely to His sole agency starting now?

Extending the Proof of Mutual Exclusion to Divine Actions
Sanusi states the conclusion and connects it to the proof of mutual exclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the same proof which shows the impossibility of a second god also demonstrates that only Allah has real effect in all actions.

Core Idea
The proof against multiple gods is also the proof against creaturely causality.

Sanusi begins by asserting that no creature has any effect. He then reveals a crucial insight: the famous proof of mutual exclusion (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) that theologians use to establish God's oneness in essence also establishes His oneness in action. This passage lays the foundation for understanding why all events are directly from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening assertion
Read the first lines of the Arabic passage: 'لا فعل لغيرِهِ سبحانَهُ ولا مؤثَّرَ سواهُ'. This is a strong negation of any action or effect for creatures.
Notice the emphatic tone.
2
Identify the connection to dalīl al-tamānuʿ
The passage states that 'بهذا الدليل' (by this proof) you know the impossibility of any creature's effect. Then it explicitly names 'دليل التمانع' and says it is the same proof that shows the necessity of Allah's oneness in actions.
This is the key extension of the proof.
3
Reflect on the scope of the negation
The negation is comprehensive: no effect in movement, stillness, obedience, disobedience, directly or indirectly. Understand that this covers all possible actions and events.
Think about how this applies to everyday causality.
4
Summarize the lesson's takeaway
The main point is that the proof of mutual exclusion is not limited to proving God's oneness in essence, but also establishes His exclusive agency in all events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
1 لا فعل لغيرِهِ سبحانَهُ ولا مؤثَّرَ سواهُ وبهذا الدليل تعرفُ استحالةَ أنْ يكونَ لشيءٍ مِنَ العالم تأثير ألبتة في أثر ما ؛ لما يلزمُ عليهِ مِنْ خروج ذلك الأثر عن قدرة مولانا جل وعزّ وإرادتِهِ ، وذلك يُوجِبُ أنْ يغلبَ الحادث القديم ، وهو محال فلا أثر إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ في حركة ولا سكون ، ولا طاعة ولا معصية، ولا في أثر ما على العموم ، لا مباشرةً ولا تولداً . يعني : أنَّ دليل التمانع الذي يدلُّ على استحالة وجودِ إلـه ثانٍ معَ مولانا جل وعزَّ هو بعينه يدلُّ على وجوبِ وحدانيته تعالى في أفعاله ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ يجب انفرادهُ تعالى باختراع جميع الحوادث بلا واسطةٍ ولا أثر لكلّ ما سواه في أثر ما على العموم . وتقرير دليل التمانعِ على هذا المطلبِ : أن نقول : لو صح أن يكون لشيء غيرِ مولانا جل وعزَّ تأثير في أثرٍ ما .. لكانَ ذلك الأثر يجبُ أنْ يكونَ مقدوراً لمولانا جل وعزَّ ومراداً لهُ ؛ لما عرفْتَ مِنْ وجوب عمومِ التعلَّقِ لإرادتِهِ تعالى وقدرته ، فإذا لزم ذلك فوقوع هذا الأثر لا يخلو : إما أن يكون لهما معاً : وهو محال ؛ لاستحالة وقوع أثر واحدٍ بمؤثرين مستقلين ؛ إذِ الفَرْضُ استقلال كلُّ واحدٍ منهما باختراع هذا الأثر من وإما أن يكونَ بأحدهما : فيلزم الترجيح بلا مُرجح ، وأيضاً يلزمُ من تخلف هذا الأثر عن أحدهما جواز تخلفه عن الآخرِ ؛ إِذِ الفَرْضُ استواؤهما بالنسبة إلى هذا الأثر ، وذلك مستلزم لجواز تعجيز قدرة المولى جل وعز وإنْ فُرِضَ ذلكَ الأثرُ لم يقع بواحدٍ منهما : لزم وقوع الحادثِ بنفسِهِ ، ولزم تعجيزُ القدرة القديمة ، وكلاهما محال هذا كله إنْ قُدْرَ توارد قدرة الإلهِ تعالى وقدرة شيء مما سواه على مقدور واحد
1 No action for other than Him, glory be to Him, and no effect besides Him. And by this proof you know the impossibility that anything from the world has any effect at all in any trace; because of what necessarily follows from it of that trace's leaving the power of our Master, glory and majesty be His, and His will, and that necessitates that the temporal event overcome the eternal, and that is impossible. So there is no effect therefore for the power of the creature in movement nor stillness, nor in obedience nor disobedience, nor in any trace at all, neither directly nor by generation. He means: that the proof of mutual exclusion (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) which indicates the impossibility of the existence of a second god alongside our Master, glory and majesty be He, is the very same that indicates the necessity of His oneness, exalted be He, in His actions; meaning: that He must be alone in inventing all temporal events without intermediary and without any effect for anything else in any trace at all. And the exposition of the proof of mutual exclusion on this point is: that we say: If it were valid that something other than our Master, glory and majesty be He, had an effect in some trace, then that trace must be within the power of our Master, glory and majesty be He, and willed by Him; because you have known the necessity of the universality of attachment for His will and power, exalted be He. So when that is necessary, then the occurrence of this trace is not free from: either it is from both together—and that is impossible, because of the impossibility of one trace occurring by two independent agents; since the assumption is the independence of each one in inventing this trace—or it is from one of them—then there would be preference without a preferrer, and also from the non-occurrence of this trace from one of them, the possibility of its non-occurrence from the other would follow, because the assumption is their equality concerning this trace, and that necessitates the possibility of rendering the power of the Master, glory and majesty be He, incapable. And if it is assumed that this trace did not occur by either one of them, then the occurrence of the temporal event by itself would be necessary, and the incapacitation of the eternal power would be necessary, and both are impossible. All this is if it is assumed that the power of Allah, exalted be He, and the power of something other than Him concur upon one object of power.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a detailed proof that no creature has any real effect. It begins with the assertion that only Allah acts and has effect. Then it states that the same proof (dalīl al-tamānuʿ) that shows the impossibility of a second god also shows the necessity of Allah's oneness in His actions. The author then presents a formal exposition: if something other than Allah had an effect, that effect would necessarily be within Allah's power and will. This leads to three exhaustive possibilities: (1) both cause it together—impossible because one effect cannot have two independent causes; (2) one causes it—which leads to preference without a reason, and also implies that if one fails, the other could also fail, thereby allowing the possibility of making Allah's power ineffective; (3) neither causes it—which would mean the event occurs by itself, also incapacitating Allah's power. All possibilities are impossible, so the premise that anything else has an effect is false. Therefore, only Allah has real effect.

Key Terms
دليل التمانع
تأثير
وحدانية الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of mutual exclusion only applies to proving that there cannot be two gods.
Correction: Sanusi explains that the same proof also shows that no creature can have any independent effect, because any effect would require a share in power and will that would lead to absurdities.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what does the proof of mutual exclusion demonstrate?
A) That there is no second god
B) That only Allah has effect in actions
C) Both A and B
D) That creatures have no power

Key Takeaway
The proof of mutual exclusion is not limited to proving God's oneness in essence, but also establishes His oneness in actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that no creature—including yourself—has any effect, how would your fear of people's opinions change? How would your reliance on your own efforts shift? Can you accept that even your obedience is not your own effect, but Allah's creation? How does that affect your gratitude and humility?
?
Think of a moment when you felt proud of an achievement. According to this lesson, that achievement was entirely Allah's action. Can you honestly say you feel no pride at all? How can you train your heart to attribute all effects to Him?
?
This lesson denies any effect for creatures, even in disobedience. Does that make you feel less guilty for your sins, or more accountable because they are created by Allah? How does this understanding change your relationship with repentance?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate

The Three Impossibilities: Why Creaturely Effect is Logically Impossible
Sanusi presents the formal exposition of the proof of mutual exclusion applied to actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that if a creature had an effect, it would lead to one of three impossible conclusions, thereby proving that only Allah is the true agent.

Core Idea
If a creature had any effect, it would either compete with Allah or render Him powerless.

Sanusi now presents the detailed logical proof. He assumes a hypothetical scenario where something other than Allah has an effect. Then he shows that this effect must be within Allah's power and will, leading to three exhaustive possibilities, each impossible. This tight argument demonstrates the impossibility of any creaturely causality.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The argument begins: if something other than Allah had an effect in some trace, that trace must be within Allah's power and will due to the universality of His attributes.
This is based on the necessity of general attachment of will and power.
2
List the three possibilities
The occurrence of the trace must either be from both together, from one of them, or from neither. These are the only exhaustive possibilities.
Memorize these three cases.
3
See why each is impossible
Both together is impossible because one effect cannot have two independent agents. One is impossible because it would require preference without a preferrer and allows incapacitation of Allah's power. Neither is impossible because the event would occur by itself, also incapacitating Allah.
Each impossibility is explained with specific reasoning.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since all three possibilities are impossible, the premise (that a creature has an effect) must be false. Therefore, no creature has any effect.
This is a classic reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

What specific action will you take today to mentally attribute the outcome to Allah alone before you start?

Which of these three impossibilities (both, one, neither) do you find yourself subconsciously falling into when you feel proud of an achievement? How does knowing this proof change your attitude toward praise from others?

Causality and Created Things
beginner

The Implication: Created Power Has No Effect
Sanusi explains the consequence of the proof: created powers are devoid of any causal effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'ari proof of God's exclusive creation implies that created powers have no independent causal effect.

Core Idea
Created powers are not causes; they are themselves created by God.

This lesson unpacks the logical consequence of the demonstration that God alone originates creation. If God creates all beings directly without intermediaries, then any power He places in creatures—like the power in animals to move—cannot be an independent cause. Sanusi draws this conclusion clearly in the passage we will examine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logical connection
Read the passage and note that it begins with 'فلا أثر إذاً' indicating a conclusion. The commentary calls it 'نتيجة' (result). This shows it follows from the previous proof.
The word 'إذاً' is a logical particle meaning 'therefore'.
2
Distinguish key terms
Understand 'قدرة المخلوق' (created power) and 'أثر' (effect). The passage denies that created power has any effect: 'لا أثر لها ألبتة'.
'أثر' means causal influence or effect in kalam terminology.
3
Reflect on the scope of denial
The denial is universal: no effect in motion, stillness, or anything else. The passage also includes the essences of animals and their powers as directly created by God.
This reinforces tawheed in causation—God is the sole creator of all actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فلا أثر إذاً لقدرةِ المخلوقِ . . . ) إلى آخره : هذا نتيجة عمَّا قبلَهُ؛ يعني : أنَّهُ لمَّا ثبت بالبرهان وجوب انفرادِهِ تعالى باختراع الكائناتِ ابتداءً بلا واسطةٍ .. لزمَ لذلكَ أنَّ القدرةَ التي خلقها الله تعالى في بعض الموجوداتِ كالحيواناتِ لا أثر لها ألبتة في حركة ولا سكون ولا غيرهما عموماً ، بل ذواتُ تلك الحيوانات ، وما فيها مِنَ القوَّةِ والقدرة ، وما صاحبَ ذلكَ مِنَ الحركة والسكون وغيرهما
His statement: 'So there is no effect, therefore, for the power of the created being...' to its end: This is a result of what preceded it; meaning: When it was established by demonstration the obligation of His uniqueness, exalted be He, in inventing existents initially without any intermediary, it follows from that that the power which God, exalted be He, created in some existents such as animals has absolutely no effect in motion or stillness or other things universally; rather, the essences of those animals, and what is in them of strength and power, and what accompanies that of motion and stillness and other things
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory note on a statement (presumably from the text being commented upon). The author identifies it as the result (نتيجة) of the preceding proof. He explains that since the proof has established that God alone originates creation without any intermediary, it necessarily follows that the power which God creates in certain beings (like animals) has no causal effect whatsoever. This power, the animal's own essence, its strength, and the accompanying motions or stillness are all created directly by God. The passage emphasizes that created powers are not independent causes; they are themselves created and their actions are creations of God.

Key Terms
أثر
قدرة المخلوق
اختراع
نتيجة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think this denies all human agency or free will, implying that humans are mere puppets with no choice.
Correction: The passage only denies independent causal efficacy; it does not deny that creatures have real power and choice that are created and sustained by God. Creatures act, but their power and actions are created by God.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why does the created power (like that in animals) have no effect?
A) Because it is weak and limited.
B) Because God alone creates all things, and He has not given any power to creatures.
C) Because the demonstration proved that God is unique in inventing existents, so any power in creatures is itself created and has no independent influence.
D) Because animals do not possess free will.

Key Takeaway
The proof of God's exclusive creation leads to the conclusion that created powers have no independent causal effect; all effects are directly from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you woke up this morning and moved your limbs, did you consciously attribute that movement to God's direct creation, or did you assume it was solely your own power? How can you train yourself to pause and recognize God's exclusive causality before every action today?
?
Consider a recent achievement you felt proud of—did your heart acknowledge that God created both your effort and the outcome? If not, what concrete step will you take to ensure your next success leads to immediate gratitude and humility before Allah?
?
If your personal power has absolutely no effect, then what basis is left for your fears about the future? Will you dare to place your complete trust in the Creator who alone causes all things, or will you continue to rely on your own illusory ability?

The Qadariyya Claim: Direct and Generated Causation
Definition of terms and exposition of Qadariyya doctrine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qadariyya doctrine of direct (mubāshara) and generated (tawallud) causation and how it attributes creative power to creatures.

Core Idea
The Qadariyya claimed human power actually invents actions, directly or through a generative chain.

Before refuting an error, we must understand it precisely. Here, Sanusi first clarifies the terms 'direct' and 'generated' causation, then presents the Qadariyya position—which he calls the 'Magians of this community'—so we can see exactly what they claimed.

Guided Path
1
Define the two terms
Read the opening lines where Sanusi explains 'no direct nor generated effect' and defines both types of causation with examples.
Direct causation = action in the same locus as power; generated = action outside that locus, like moving a stone via hand.
2
Identify the Qadariyya claim
Notice how the Qadariyya assert that created power invents actions, both directly (bodily movements) and by generation (external effects).
They consider the servant as the real inventor, with secondary causes like nerve strength affecting the outcome.
3
Understand their examples
Reflect on their examples: moving a stone (generated) is said to arise from hand movement which they consider directly caused.
This shows their belief in a causal chain originating from the creature's power.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال القول بتأثير ما سوى الله تعالى بالمباشرة والتولد ] قوله : ( لا مباشرةً ولا تولُّداً ) يعني : أنَّه لا فرق في عدم تأثيرِ القدرةِ الحادثةِ بينَ الفعل الذي وُجِدَ معَها في محلّ واحدٍ ؛ كحركة يد المختار مثلاً ، وبين الفعل الذي يُوجَدُ خارجاً عن محلها ؛ كحركة المفتاح والسيف مثلاً عند حركة اليد ، وهو الذي يُعنى بالتولُّدِ ، ونبَّهَ بهذا على مذهب القدرية مجوس هذهِ الأمَّةِ - أبعدَهم الله تعالى - حيث قالوا : إنَّ القدرة الحادثة والقوَّةَ التي خلق الله تعالى في الحيوانِ هي التي بها يخترع الحيوان أفعاله على وفق ما يريدُ . قالوا - أهلكَهمُ اللهُ تعالى - : فمنها ما يخترعه بها مباشرةً ؛ أي : واسطة ؛ وذلكَ كحركاتِ ذاتِهِ وسكناتها التي في محلّ قدرته وقوته ، ومنها ما يخترعُهُ بها تولُّداً ؛ أي : بواسطة ؛ وذلك كتحريكه الحجرَ أوِ السيفَ ، أو رميه بالسهم ونحوه ، أو جَرْحِهِ لشخص ونحو ذلك ، فإِنَّ هذهِ الأشياءَ قالوا - أبعدَهم الله تعالى - : العبد هو الذي يخترعُها بقوَّتِهِ ، لكن لا مباشرةً ، بل بواسطة اختراعه حركةً في يدِهِ ، واعتماداً بها على ذلكَ ، قالوا - أهلكهم الله تعالى - : ويختلفُ الأثر في ذلكَ بحَسَبِ اختلافِ قوَّةِ العصب وضعفِهِ . ولهذا كانَتْ حقيقةُ التولدِ عندَهم وجود حادث عن مقدور بالقدرةِ الحادثة ، فحركة الحجرِ مثلاً مُتولّدةٌ عندَهم ؛ لأنَّها حادث نشأ عن شيء مقدور بالقدرة الحادثة ، وهو حركة اليد والاعتماد بها . ولأهل الحقِّ معهم كلام وأدلَّةٌ خاصة بالتولدِ ، أبانوا فيها عوارَهم وخِسَّةَ عقولهم على تقدير تسليم أصلهم الفاسد في تأثير القدرة الحادثة مباشرةً ، وقد ذكرنا كثيراً منها في «العقيدة الكبرى وشرحها » ، فلينظر هنالك . ويكفي هنا باختصار : أَنَّهُ لمَّا اتَّضحَ أَنَّ القدرة الحادثة لا أثر لها ألبتةَ فيما يُوجَدُ في محلّها مِنَ الأفعالِ .. كانَ عدمُ تأثيرها فيما ليس في محلها ـ كحركة الحجر والسيف ونحوهما ـ أحرى . وبالجملة : فالذي عليهِ أهلُ الحقِّ الذينَ مَنَّ الله تعالى عليهم بالبراءةِ مِنْ أنواع الشركِ كلَّها ، ونور قلوبهم بحقيقة التوحيد المُنجية بفَضْلِ اللهِ تعالى مِنَ الخلودِ في العذابِ الشديد.. أَنَّهُ لا أثرَ لمخلوق أي مخلوقٍ كانَ في أثر ما عموماً ، لا بالمباشرة ولا بالتولد ؛ أي : لا بغير واسطة ولا بواسطةٍ ، وما وُجِدَ معَ قوَّةِ مخلوقٍ وقدرتِهِ مِنَ الأفعال ، سواءٌ وُجِدَ في ذاتِهِ ؛ كحركاتِهِ وسكناته ، أو مصاحباً لما هو خارج عنه ؛ كحركات الحجر والرمح والسهم واندفاعها ، وكحركة السيف والجراحاتِ المقارنة لذلك ونحو ذلك . . إِنَّما هو واقع بمحْضِ خَلْقِ اللهِ تعالى واختياره بلا واسطة ولا سببٍ ، وإِنَّما هو جلَّ وعزَّ يجمع بين ما يشاءُ مِنْ مخلوقاتِهِ ، ويُفرِّقُ بين ما يشاء تبارك وتعالى
Refutation of the claim of effect from other than Allah Almighty directly (mubāsharatan) and by generation (tawallud). His statement: 'neither directly nor by generation' means: there is no difference in the non-effect of the originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) between the act that occurs with it in a single locus—like the movement of the hand of the one who chooses, for example—and the act that occurs outside its locus—like the movement of the key and the sword, for example, upon the movement of the hand—and this is what is meant by generation (al-tawallud). And he pointed by this to the doctrine of the Qadariyya, the Magians of this community—may Allah Almighty remove them—where they said: indeed the originated power and the strength that Allah Almighty created in the animal are that by which the animal invents its actions according to what it wills. They said—may Allah Almighty destroy them—: among them are what it invents by it directly, i.e., without intermediary; and that is like the movements of its self and its stillnesses that are in the locus of its power and strength. And among them are what it invents by it by generation, i.e., with an intermediary; and that is like its moving the stone or the sword, or its shooting an arrow and the like, or its wounding a person and the like. For these things, they said—may Allah Almighty remove them—: the servant is the one who invents them by his strength, but not directly, rather by means of his invention of a movement in his hand, and relying by it upon that. They said—may Allah Almighty destroy them—: and the effect differs in that according to the difference of the strength of the nerve and its weakness. And for this reason, the reality of generation according to them is the existence of an event from something within the capacity of the originated power. So the movement of the stone, for example, is generational according to them, because it is an event that arose from something within the capacity of the originated power, namely the movement of the hand and the reliance upon it. And the People of Truth have with them speech and proofs specific to generation, in which they exposed their faults and the baseness of their minds, assuming the acceptance of their corrupt principle concerning the effect of the originated power directly. And we have mentioned many of them in 'al-ʿAqīda al-Kubrā and its commentary', so let one look there. And it suffices here briefly: that when it became clear that the originated power has absolutely no effect in the acts that occur in its locus, then its non-effect in what is not in its locus—like the movement of the stone and the sword and the like—is more fitting. And in summary: what the People of Truth—whom Allah Almighty has favored with immunity from all kinds of polytheism and illuminated their hearts with the reality of tawḥīd that saves, by the grace of Allah Almighty, from eternal severe punishment—hold is: that there is no effect for any creature whatsoever, generally, neither directly nor by generation; i.e., neither without intermediary nor with intermediary. And whatever acts occur with the strength and power of a creature, whether they occur in its own self—like its movements and stillnesses—or accompanying what is outside it—like the movements of the stone, the spear, the arrow and their propulsion, and like the movement of the sword and the accompanying wounds and the like—that is only occurring by the sheer creation of Allah Almighty and His choice, without intermediary or cause. And He, glorified and exalted, only combines whatever He wills among His creatures and separates whatever He wills, blessed and exalted.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a refutation (ibṭāl) of the claim that anything other than Allah Almighty has any effect on actions, whether directly (mubāsharatan) or by generation (tawallud). It begins by clarifying the meaning of the statement 'neither directly nor by generation' from the author's earlier text. The key point is that the originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) has no effect at all, regardless of whether the act occurs in the same locus as the power (like moving one's own hand) or outside it (like moving a key or sword through hand movement). The latter type is what is meant by 'generation' (tawallud). The author then connects this to the erroneous doctrine of the Qadariyya (the 'Magians of this community'), who claim that the created power and strength in animals actually invents their actions according to their will. They divide actions into two categories: those invented directly (mubāshara), without intermediary, such as the animal's own movements; and those invented by generation (tawallud), with an intermediary, such as moving a stone or wounding someone. According to them, the servant invents the latter not directly but through first inventing a movement in his hand and then relying on it to produce the external effect. They even claim that the effect varies based on the strength or weakness of the nerves. The author then explains that the reality of generation according to them is the existence of an event that arises from something that is within the capacity of the originated power. For example, the movement of the stone is 'generational' because it arises from the movement of the hand, which they consider directly caused. The People of Truth (Ahl al-Ḥaqq) have detailed arguments against this notion of generation, which the author says are recorded in his larger work al-ʿAqīda al-Kubrā and its commentary. For the present context, a brief argument suffices: since it is already established that originated power has absolutely no effect even on acts within its own locus, it is even more obvious that it has no effect on acts outside its locus (like stone or sword movement). The passage concludes with a summary of the correct Ashʿarī position: no creature has any effect whatsoever on any action, whether directly or through generation. All acts that are observed with a creature's power—whether internal (like its own movements) or external (like the movement of a stone or a sword)—are brought into existence solely by Allah's direct creation and choice, without any intermediary or independent cause. Allah simply combines or separates His created things as He wills. This doctrine guards against the subtle polytheism of attributing causal efficacy to creatures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That created beings can cause effects independently through a generative chain originating from their own power.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Ḥaqq, no creature has any effect at all; all actions are created directly by Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the Qadariyya as described in this passage, how does a wound caused by a sword occur?
A) Allah creates the wound directly without any creature's involvement
B) The servant invents the wound directly by his power
C) The servant invents the wound through generation: first inventing hand movement, then relying on it to produce the wound
D) The sword itself has independent power to cause wounds

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya assert that creatures have real causal power, either directly or through a generative chain, which fundamentally compromises tawḥīd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you accomplish something difficult—like completing a project or overcoming a temptation—do you instinctively thank Allah for creating the action, or do you silently congratulate your own will and effort? This lesson reveals that attributing real causal power to yourself is exactly what the Qadariyya did. What one thought pattern will you consciously redirect to Allah today?
?
Recall a moment you felt angry or resentful toward someone for something they did to you. In that moment, did you assume that person had the independent power to harm you? According to this lesson, only Allah creates actions. How does acknowledging that change your response? What will you do the next time you feel wronged?
?
Is there an area of your life—work, health, relationships—where you act as if your success depends primarily on your own choices and abilities? This lesson calls that a violation of tawheed. What concrete prayer or practice can you adopt to remind yourself that Allah is the sole creator of every outcome, including your next heartbeat?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
The Ash'ari Refutation: No Effect from Creatures
Refutation of Qadariyya and summary of Ash'ari doctrine on causality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari refutation of the Qadariyya claim and the correct doctrine that all actions are created solely by Allah.

Core Idea
Since created power has no effect even on acts within its own locus, it certainly has no effect on external acts.

Having laid out the Qadariyya error, Sanusi now delivers the decisive refutation. He first notes that the People of Truth have detailed arguments elsewhere, but here he provides a succinct logical proof: if created power has no effect in its own locus, then even more so it has no effect outside that locus.

Guided Path
1
Follow the logical argument
Read the brief argument: since created power has zero effect on its own locus (already proven), then it is even more fitting that it has no effect outside—like moving a stone.
This is a simple 'a fortiori' (awlā) argument.
2
Understand the summary of correct belief
Read the concluding statement: no creature has any effect whatsoever, directly or by generation. All actions are created by Allah alone without intermediary or cause.
This is the definitive Ash'ari position.
3
Reflect on the nature of Tawḥīd
Note that this doctrine guards against hidden polytheism by denying any independent causal power to creatures.
All apparent causal links are simply Allah's habit of creating things in sequence.

According to them, the servant invents the latter not directly but through first inventing a movement in his hand and then relying on it to produce the external effect. They even claim that the effect varies based on the strength or weakness of the nerves. The author then explains that the reality of generation according to them is the existence of an event that arises from something that is within the capacity of the originated power. For example, the movement of the stone is 'generational' because it arises from the movement of the hand, which they consider directly caused. The People of Truth (Ahl al-Ḥaqq) have detailed arguments against this notion of generation, which the author says are recorded in his larger work al-ʿAqīda al-Kubrā and its commentary. For the present context, a brief argument suffices: since it is already established that originated power has absolutely no effect even on acts within its own locus, it is even more obvious that it has no effect on acts outside its locus (like stone or sword movement). The passage concludes with a summary of the correct Ashʿarī position: no creature has any effect whatsoever on any action, whether directly or through generation. All acts that are observed with a creature's power—whether internal (like its own movements) or external (like the movement of a stone or a sword)—are brought into existence solely by Allah's direct creation and choice, without any intermediary or independent cause. Allah simply combines or separates His created things as He wills. This doctrine guards against the subtle polytheism of attributing causal efficacy to creatures.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة
أهل الحق
الاختراع
المباشرة
التولد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the People of Truth, how should we understand actions that appear to be caused by creatures, like a wound from a sword?
A) The creature's power creates the wound indirectly through generation
B) The creature's power creates the wound directly
C) Allah creates the wound directly, without any causal role of the creature
D) The sword's sharpness combined with the creature's strength causes the wound

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position affirms that no creature has any causal efficacy; all that happens is directly created by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you thank someone for a favor, do you really believe in your heart that their action had no effect, and that Allah alone created the benefit? What will you do differently to make this conviction real in your gratitude?
?
Think of a recent moment when you felt proud of your own effort or skill. How does this lesson strip away that pride and redirect all power to Allah? What daily habit can you adopt to remind yourself that your abilities have no intrinsic effect?
?
If tomorrow you face a situation where all human means fail, will you truly trust that Allah’s direct creation is sufficient, or will you despair? What is one concrete step you can take right now to strengthen that trust based on this lesson?

Refutation of Tawallud and Creaturely Non-Effect
Sanusi refutes tawallud and states Ash'ari position on creaturely non-effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari argument that creatures have no causal effect whatsoever, neither directly nor indirectly, and that all apparent causation is direct divine creation.

Core Idea
No creature has any effect; all is direct from Allah.

This lesson presents Sanusi's concise refutation of the Mu'tazilite theory of tawallud (generated causation). After referencing fuller arguments elsewhere, he gives a brief but powerful argument: if created power has no effect even in its own locus, it certainly has no effect outside it. The lesson then states the Ash'ari principle of absolute creaturely non-effect.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The Mu'tazilites held that creatures can cause effects indirectly (tawallud). Sanusi begins by noting that the Ahl al-Haqq have detailed proofs elsewhere, but here gives a concise refutation.
2
Follow the key argument
If created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) has no effect on actions occurring in its own locus (the body), then it is even more certain that it has no effect on things outside its locus, like the movement of a stone or sword.
This is an a fortiori argument.
3
Grasp the summary principle
No creature, any creature, has any effect on any effect, whether directly or indirectly. Any appearance of causation is actually Allah creating both the action and its concomitant effects.
The principle is stated both generally and with examples.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
This establishes pure divine agency and removes any notion of secondary causation, guarding against shirk. Allah simply brings together and separates His creatures as He wills.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأهل الحقِّ معهم كلام وأدلَّةٌ خاصة بالتولدِ ، أبانوا فيها عوارَهم وخِسَّةَ عقولهم على تقدير تسليم أصلهم الفاسد في تأثير القدرة الحادثة مباشرةً ، وقد ذكرنا كثيراً منها في «العقيدة الكبرى وشرحها » ، فلينظر هنالك (١) ويكفي هنا باختصار : أَنَّهُ لمَّا اتَّضحَ أَنَّ القدرة الحادثة لا أثر لها ألبتةَ فيما يُوجَدُ في محلّها مِنَ الأفعالِ .. كانَ عدمُ تأثيرها فيما ليس في محلها ـ كحركة الحجر والسيف ونحوهما ـ أحرى وبالجملة : فالذي عليهِ أهلُ الحقِّ الذينَ مَنَّ الله تعالى عليهم بالبراءةِ مِنْ أنواع الشركِ كلَّها (۲) ، ونور قلوبهم بحقيقة التوحيد المُنجية بفَضْلِ اللهِ تعالى مِنَ الخلودِ في العذابِ الشديد.. أَنَّهُ لا أثرَ لمخلوق أي مخلوقٍ كانَ في أثر ما عموماً ، لا بالمباشرة ولا بالتولد ؛ أي : لا بغير واسطة ولا بواسطةٍ ، وما وُجِدَ معَ قوَّةِ مخلوقٍ وقدرتِهِ مِنَ سواءٌ [؟] وُجِدَ في ذاتِهِ ؛ كحركاتِهِ وسكناته ، أو مصاحباً لما [؟] الأفعال ، سوا وُجِدَ في ذاتِهِ ؛ كحركات الحجر والرمح والسهم واندفاعها ، وكحركة السيف والجراحاتِ المقارنة لذلك ونحو ذلك . . إِنَّما هو واقع بمحْضِ خَلْقِ اللهِ تعالى واختياره بلا واسطة ولا سببٍ(٣) ، وإِنَّما هو جلَّ وعزَّ يجمع بين ما يشاءُ مِنْ مخلوقاتِهِ ، ويُفرِّقُ بين ما يشاء تبارك وتعالى
And the people of truth have with them discourse and proofs specific to tawallud, in which they exposed their defects and the baseness of their intellects on the assumption of conceding their corrupt principle in the effect of the originated power directly. And we have mentioned many of them in al-ʿAqīda al-Kubrā and its commentary, so let one look there (1). And it suffices here briefly: that when it became clear that the originated power has absolutely no effect in the actions that occur in its locus, then its non-effect in what is not in its locus—like the movement of the stone and the sword and the like—is more fitting. And in summary: that which the people of truth—whom Allah Almighty has favored with freedom from all kinds of shirk, and illuminated their hearts with the reality of tawḥīd that saves, by the grace of Allah Almighty, from eternal severe punishment—hold is that there is no effect for any creature whatsoever in any effect generally, neither directly nor by tawallud; that is, neither without intermediary nor with intermediary. And whatever exists with the strength of a creature and its power—whether it exists in its essence, like its movements and stillnesses, or accompanying [؟] the actions, equally existing in its essence, like the movements of the stone, spear, arrow and their propulsion, and like the movement of the sword and the wounds concomitant to that and the like—is only occurring by the sheer creation of Allah Almighty and His choice, without intermediary or cause (3). And He, Glorious and Exalted, only brings together what He wills of His creatures and separates what He wills, Blessed and Exalted.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a concise refutation of the Mu'tazilite theory of tawallud (secondary causation) and a summary statement of the Ash'ari position on the non-effect of creatures. Sanusi begins by noting that the Ahl al-Haqq have detailed arguments against the Mu'tazilites on this issue, which he has recorded elsewhere. He then gives a brief argument: if the created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) has absolutely no effect even on actions occurring in its own locus (the human body), then it is even more certain that it has no effect on things outside its locus, like the movement of a stone or a sword. He then states the general principle: no creature has any effect on any effect (athar) whatsoever, whether directly (mubāshara) or indirectly (tawallud). Whatever appears alongside a creature's power—whether within the creature itself (like its own movements) or accompanying external objects (like the movement of a stone, spear, arrow, or sword and the wounds they cause)—is in fact created directly by Allah without any intermediary or cause. Allah merely brings together and separates His creatures as He wills. This passage guards against the misconception that creatures can be real agents of effects, whether by direct or indirect causation.

Key Takeaway
Creatures have absolutely no causal effect; all apparent causation is direct divine creation without intermediary.

The passage says creatures have no effect 'generally'. This includes the harm others cause you. How does this truth affect your response when someone wrongs you? Can you truly see them as mere instruments of Allah's decree and not as independent agents deserving of resentment? Would you forgive more readily if you believed they had no causal power to harm you?

The Limited Scope of Created Power
Sanusi explains that created power attaches only to certain acts, not all possibles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that created power (qudra haditha) only relates to certain types of acts, not to all possible things.

Core Idea
Created power is not a universal capacity—it attaches only to specific acts like movement and thought.

Sanusi now refines our understanding of created power by specifying its scope. Although we learned that it is non-effecting, we might think it could at least relate to everything. This passage corrects that misunderstanding: created power only relates to a subset of acts, such as voluntary motions and intellectual acts, not to things beyond the agent's sphere.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the contrast between what power relates to and what it does not.
The passage uses 'for example' to indicate the list is not exhaustive.
2
Identify what power does NOT relate to
The passage explicitly says power does not relate to a person's color. Why is that a clear example? Because color is not an act of the servant.
3
Identify what power DOES relate to
Movement and stillness are mentioned as examples. The commentator adds that intellectual acts like reflection and belief also fall under its relation.
Notice the phrase 'for example' in the original creed.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this limitation matters: it shows that human power is not a creative force but rather a capacity tied to specific types of actions.
This connects to the idea that only God creates, while humans merely acquire.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And this power – while it is non-effecting – is not suitable to relate to every possible thing, nor to everything that God most high creates from possible things in ourselves; for when God creates it in the servant, for example, we know necessarily that it has not related to his color, while it has related to his movement and stillness. And his saying in the original creed: 'for example,' after his saying: 'like movement and stillness' is an indication that it may relate to other than movement and stillness, like intellectual consideration, knowledge, opinion, belief, and so forth.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage clarifies the scope of the created power's relation (ta'allaq). Although it has no effect, it is not omnirelational: it attaches to some acts but not others. For instance, a person's power does not relate to the color of his skin but does relate to his voluntary movements and stillness. The commentator notes that Sanusi's use of 'for example' indicates that the relation extends beyond physical acts to mental acts such as intellectual reflection (al-nazr al-fikri), knowledge, opinion, and belief.

Objection and Answer on Taklif in External Acts
The commentator addresses the objection that taklif applies to acts outside human power, like jihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari concept of acquisition resolves the objection that sharia obligations sometimes command acts beyond human power, by distinguishing between the external act and its customary cause within human ability.

Core Idea
Sharia obligates the acquired means, not the external effect.

This passage presents a common objection against the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition: how can Allah command acts like jihad that involve effects beyond the servant's power? The objector argues that human power only extends to actions within the body. The answer distinguishes between the external act (e.g., killing) and the acquired action (e.g., striking), which Allah has made the customary cause of the external event. Thus, the obligation is on what the servant can do, not on what is beyond his power.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Begin by reading the objector's statement in Arabic and translation. Notice the examples given: jihad, restraining sinners, and prohibiting unjust harm.
The objector is someone who does not accept that obligation can attach to acts without kasb.
2
Identify the objector's argument
The objector argues that originated power only attaches by acquisition to actions within its own locus (the servant's body). External effects are beyond that locus, so they cannot be directly obligated.
Locus (محل) means the site of power, i.e., the body.
3
Read the commentator's answer
The commentator responds that the obligation in those external matters is actually on the acquired movements and stillness of the servant, which Allah has made customary causes for those external events.
Customary cause (سبب عادي) means the regular occurrence by God's custom.
4
Reflect on the resolution
Consider how this preserves both divine justice (no obligation beyond ability) and human responsibility (the servant is commanded to perform the acquired action that leads to the external result).
This resolution is a key aspect of the Ash'ari theory of acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : قد وجدنا التكليف ثابتاً فيما لا كسب للعبد فيه ؛ كوجوب جهادِ الكفَّارِ بالضرب والقتل ، ووجوب زجْرِ الفُسَّاقِ والمحاربين بمثل ذلك ، وكتحريم قتل أو ضرب مَنْ لا يستحق الضرب أو القتل ، ونحو ذلك ، فإنَّ القدرة الحادثة لا تتعلق على طريق الاكتساب إلا بما وُجِدَ في محلّها مِنَ الأفعالِ ، أَمَّا ما خرجَ عن محلّها فلا تعلُّق لها به أصلاً . قلتُ : التكليفُ في تلك الأمور الخارجة عن محل قدرةِ العبدِ إِنَّما واقع بالمكتسب للعبدِ مِنْ حركاته وسكناته ونحوهما ، مما أجرى الله تعالى العادةَ أنْ يُوجِدَ عندَهُ تلك الأمورَ ؛ فحيثُ ورد في الشرع تكليف بشيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ فإنَّ المراد منهُ إِنَّما هو التكليف بسببه العادي المقدور للعبد المكتسب له ، والله أعلم .
If you say: 'We have found obligation established in something that has no kasb for the servant, such as the obligation of jihad against disbelievers by striking and killing, and the obligation of restraining sinners and rebels by similar means, and the prohibition of killing or striking someone who does not deserve striking or killing, and the like. For the originated power does not attach by way of acquisition except to what exists in its locus of actions. As for what exits its locus, it has no attachment to it at all.' I say: 'The obligation in those matters external to the locus of the servant's power is only actually by what is acquired for the servant from his movements, stillness, and the like, which Allah has established by custom to create those matters at their occurrence. So wherever in the sharia an obligation regarding something of that kind occurs, the intended meaning is only obligation by its customary cause which is within the servant's power and acquired by him. And Allah knows best.'
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer format common in kalam texts. The objector raises a problem: we find sharia obligations that involve acts outside the servant's power, like striking a disbeliever in jihad or restraining a wrongdoer. The objector argues that the servant's originated power only attaches by way of acquisition to actions within its own locus (i.e., the servant's own body), not to external effects like the pain caused to another or the act of killing. So how can such obligations be just? The commentator answers by explaining that the obligation in these external matters is actually directed at the acquired actions of the servant (his movements and stillness) that are the customary causes of those external events. According to God's custom, these external events are created when the servant performs his acquired actions. Thus, the sharia obligation is to perform the acquired action (e.g., striking) which is within the servant's power, and the external result is not directly obligated. This preserves the principle that obligation only applies to what is within human ability.

Key Terms
اكتساب (acquisition)
قدرة حادثة (originated power)
عادة (custom)
سبب عادي (customary cause)
محل (locus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that sharia obligates impossible acts if it commands causing external harm, because such acts are beyond human power.
Correction: The obligation is on the acquired means (e.g., striking) that are within human power and are the customary causes of the external effects.

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the objection that jihad obligates acts outside the servant's power?
A) By denying that such acts are truly obligated.
B) By claiming that the servant's power extends to everything.

D) By arguing that the sharia only obligates internal intentions, not external actions.

Key Takeaway
This passage shows that the Ash'ari concept of acquisition resolves the problem of divine command over external acts by focusing on the customary cause within human power.

The Definition of Kasb and the Two Proofs
Sanusi defines kasb and lists the two proofs for it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of kasb as an accompanying power without effect, and the two proofs (scriptural and rational) that Ahl al-Haqq use to establish it.

Core Idea
Kasb means our actions are accompanied by a powerless capacity.

Sanusi begins by defining kasb as an originated power that accompanies voluntary action without influencing it. He then mentions two proofs—one from revelation and one from reason—that support this doctrine. The scriptural proof is brief, while the rational proof is developed in detail in the next lesson.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of kasb
Carefully read the opening lines. Notice the key phrase: 'without having any effect in it at all'—this is the crucial point.
Kasb does not mean human creation; it is an accompaniment.
2
Identify the two proofs
After the definition, Sanusi states there are two proofs. The first is scriptural, the second rational. Understand that the scriptural proof is based on the Law only obligating acquired actions.
3
Note the rational proof's starting point
The rational proof begins with the necessary perception of a difference between voluntary and involuntary movements. This distinction is the foundation for the detailed argument in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يعني: أنَّ أهلَ الحقِّ استدلُّوا على ثبوتِ الكسب للعبدِ؛ بمعنى: أنَّ فعلَهُ الاختياري ـ أي: الذي يصح منه في العادة تركه وفعلُهُ - تصاحبه عند وجودِهِ فيهِ قدرةٌ حادثةٌ تتعلَّقُ بهِ مِنْ غير تأثير لها فيه أصلاً . . بدليلين
أحدهما: شرعيٌّ: وقد أشار إليه فيما سبق؛ وهو أنَّ الشرعَ إنَّما كلَّفَ بالمكتسب مِنَ الأفعالِ دون غيرها .
الثاني: عقلي: وهو ما أشرنا إليه هنا مِنْ إدراكنا الفَرْقَ ضرورةً بين حركة الاضطرارِ؛ كحركةِ الرَّعْشَةِ أو تحريك الغيرِ يدَنا ونحوِ ذلك، وبين حركة الاختيار؛ وهي الحركة التي يتمكَّنُ عادةً مِنْ فعلها وتركها
ولنفرض هاتين الحركتين متحدتين في الجهة والحيز حتى يتماثلا، فنقولُ في سَبْرِ سببِ الفرقِ الضروري بينهما: لا يصح أنْ ترجعَ التفرقة بينهما إلى نفس الحركة وحقيقتها؛ لفَرْضِ تماثلهما،
ولا إلى نفس ذاتِ المتحرِّكِ؛ لأنَّ معقول ذاتِهِ في الحالتين واحدٌ،
فتعيَّنَ أنْ ترجعَ التفرقةُ إلى صفةٍ زائدة في المتحرك المختارِ
ثم يبطل رجوعُها إلى حالٍ؛ لأنَّ الحال لا تطرأُ بمُجرَّدِها على الجوهر
وإنْ كانَتْ عَرَضاً: فإمَّا أنْ تكونَ ممَّا يُشترَطُ في ثبوتها الحياة أو لا، ويمتنع رجوعُها إلى صفة لا يُشترط في ثبوتها الحياةُ؛ إذْ لا يتصف بالحركة الاختياريَّةِ مَنْ ليسَ بحي، فوجب أن ترجع التفرقة إلى معنى يُشترط في ثبوتِهِ الحياةُ .
ويبطل كونه علماً أو حياةً أو كلاماً؛ إذ الكل يُوجَدُ مع الحركة الاضطرارية، بل مع عدم الحركة أصلاً .
ويبطل كونه إرادة؛ لأنَّ الحركة الاختيارية موجودة ولا إرادة؛ وذلكَ معَ النُّهولِ والنوم ونحوهما .
لا يُقالُ: لا تُسلَّمُ أنَّ الحركة في هذه الأحوالِ اختيارية .
لأنَّا نقولُ: لا خفاءَ أنَّ هذهِ الحركة ليسَتْ باضطراريَّةٍ، فتعيَّنَ أَنْ تكون اختيارية، وليس المعني بالاختياريَّةِ إِلا كونَها يُتَمَكَّنُ مِنْ فعلها وتركها عادةً، وذلكَ موجود في هذه الأحوالِ
He means: The people of truth adduced evidence for the affirmation of acquisition (al-kasb) for the servant; meaning: that his voluntary action – i.e., that which it is normally possible for him to leave and do – is accompanied, at its occurrence in him, by an originated power (qudratun ḥādithatun) that is related to it without having any effect in it at all... by two proofs: one, scriptural: he [previously] indicated it earlier; it is that the Law only obligated the acquired (al-muktasab) of actions, not others. Second, rational: that which we indicated here, namely our necessarily perceiving the difference between the involuntary movement – like the movement of tremor or someone else moving our hand and the like – and the voluntary movement, which is the movement that one is normally able to do and leave. Let us suppose these two movements are united in direction (jiha) and locus (ḥayz) such that they are similar; then we say in probing the cause of the necessary difference between them: It is not valid that the differentiation between them goes back to the movement itself and its essence, because of the assumption of their similarity; nor to the essence of the mover itself, because the intelligible of its essence in both states is one. So it is determined that the differentiation goes back to an additional attribute in the voluntary mover. Then it is invalid that it goes back to a state (ḥāl), because the state does not occur by its mere self upon the substance (jawhar). And if it is an accident (ʿaraḍ): then either it is something whose existence requires life or not, and it is impossible that it goes back to an attribute whose existence does not require life, since one who is not living is not described with voluntary movement. So it is necessary that the differentiation goes back to a meaning whose existence requires life. And it is invalid that it is knowledge, life, or speech, because all are found with involuntary movement, even with no movement at all. And it is invalid that it is will (irāda), because voluntary movement exists without will; that is in the case of emaciation (nuhūl), sleep, and the like. It cannot be said: "It is not granted that movement in these states is voluntary." Because we say: There is no concealment that this movement is not involuntary, so it is determined that it is voluntary. And the meaning of 'voluntary' is nothing other than that one is normally able to do and leave it, and that exists in these states.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage presents the rational proof for the doctrine of kasb (acquisition) as held by Ahl al-Haqq. The author begins by defining kasb: the servant's voluntary action is accompanied by an originated power (qudratun ḥādithatun) that relates to the action without having any effect on it. This definition frames the problem. Then two proofs are given: a scriptural proof (the Law only obligates acquired actions) and a rational proof, which is the focus. The rational proof starts from our necessary perception of a difference between involuntary movements (like tremor) and voluntary movements (those one can normally do or leave). The author asks us to assume both movements are identical in direction and locus, making them similar in essence. Then, in searching for the cause of the necessary difference, he eliminates the movement itself (because they are assumed identical) and the mover's essence (because the essence is the same in both cases). Thus the difference must be due to an additional attribute in the voluntary mover. Next, he eliminates the possibility that this attribute is a state (ḥāl), because a state does not arise independently in a substance. If it is an accident, it must require life for its existence, because only a living being can perform voluntary movement. This attribute cannot be knowledge, life, or speech, since these exist even with involuntary movement or absence of movement. Nor can it be will (irāda), because voluntary movement can occur without will, as in cases of extreme emaciation, sleep, and the like. An objection is raised: are those movements truly voluntary? The answer affirms they are not involuntary, and the definition of voluntary (ability to do or leave normally) applies. Therefore, the attribute must be an originated power (the capacity for acquisition). The argument tightly follows the method of elimination and relies on necessary empirical distinctions.

Key Terms
كسب (kasb)
قدرة حادثة (originated power)
اختيار (voluntary)
اضطرار (involuntary)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Kasb means humans create their own actions.
Correction: Kasb means an accompanying power without effect, not creation.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the role of the originated power in the servant's voluntary action?
A) It creates the action.
B) It accompanies the action without effect.
C) It causes the action.
D) It determines the action.

Key Takeaway
Kasb is the orthodox doctrine that human actions are accompanied by a power from God that has no effect, preserving divine omnipotence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you truly feel that God alone created that action, and your 'acquisition' adds nothing? How would your humility increase if you acknowledged your powerlessness in every moment of obedience? Will you commit to whispering a reminder to yourself before each act: 'This is from Allah, not from me'?
?
The passage says the difference between voluntary and involuntary is 'necessarily perceived'. But when you sin, do you not secretly feel that you could have done otherwise—that your own power made the difference? How can you train your heart to see that even your worst actions are accompanied by a power that has no effect, yet you are still responsible? Will you repent today with the awareness that your repentance itself is an acquired action sustained by God?
?
The Law only obligates acquired actions. Are there areas of your life where you treat religious obligations as mechanical (like tremors) rather than as opportunities to consciously acquire them? What would change if you approached every prayer and charity as a voluntary acquisition that you could leave, but you choose it only by God's grace?

8 min
The Rational Proof for Kasb: Elimination Argument
Sanusi presents the rational proof for kasb by eliminating other possible causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for kasb through a process of elimination, showing that the difference between voluntary and involuntary movement must be due to an originated power.

Core Idea
The difference between voluntary and involuntary movement can only be an originated power.

Sanusi now develops the rational proof he introduced earlier. He sets up a thought experiment: suppose two movements are identical in all respects except one is voluntary and the other involuntary. The difference cannot be in the movement itself or the mover's essence, so it must be an additional attribute. By eliminating state, knowledge, life, speech, and will, he concludes that the attribute must be an originated power (qudratun hadithatun), which is the capacity for acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the initial assumption
Imagine two movements that are identical in direction and locus—one voluntary, one involuntary. This isolates the difference.
The assumption of similarity forces us to look beyond the movement itself.
2
Follow the elimination process
Read how Sanusi eliminates the movement itself, the mover's essence, a 'state', and then attributes that do not require life.
Each step is based on a logical impossibility or empirical observation.
3
Examine the elimination of will (irāda)
Sanusi argues that voluntary movement occurs without will in cases like sleep and emaciation, so the difference cannot be will.
This is a key argument against the Ash'ari claim that will is the cause.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An opponent might deny that movements in sleep are voluntary. Sanusi defends their voluntary nature because they are not involuntary and meet the definition of being able to do or leave normally.
This shows the robustness of the proof.

يعني: أنَّ أهلَ الحقِّ استدلُّوا على ثبوتِ الكسب للعبدِ؛ بمعنى: أنَّ فعلَهُ الاختياري ـ أي: الذي يصح منه في العادة تركه وفعلُهُ - تصاحبه عند وجودِهِ فيهِ قدرةٌ حادثةٌ تتعلَّقُ بهِ مِنْ غير تأثير لها فيه أصلاً . . بدليلين

The Correct Ash'ari Position: Created Power Has No Effect
The author states the correct Ash'ari position and warns against deviating from it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the standard Ash'ari position is that created power has absolutely no effect, and that any other opinion is not relied upon.

Core Idea
Created power is not effective; only Allah creates.

This lesson clarifies the foundational Ash'ari teaching on causality: created beings have no true causal power. The author warns against accepting other opinions attributed to Ash'ari scholars, emphasizing that the well-known position is the only valid one both intellectually and legally.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning and correct position
Read the passage where the author states the well-known position: created power has absolutely no effect. Notice the strong language: 'cannot be valid intellectually or legally to contradict.'
2
Identify the source of authority
Understand that the author is presenting this as the only reliable view from Ahl al-Sunna. Other opinions are not to be relied upon.
3
Connect to broader Ash'ari theology
Reflect on how this position supports occasionalism, where all effective power belongs to Allah alone.
This is a key point in Ash'ari kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه
على أقوال أعلام مِنْ أهل السنَّةِ ليس عليها المُعوَّلُ
ما اقتصرنا عليه في أصلِ العقيدةِ مِنْ عدم التأثير للقدرة الحادثة ألبتة هو المعروفُ المشهورُ عندَهم ، الذي لا يصح عقلاً ولا شرعاً خلافه ، وبعضُ مَنْ أُولعَ بنقل الغثّ والسمينِ مِنَ الأقوال .. ينقلُ هنا أقوالاً أُخَرَ ينسبها لأهل السنَّةِ أيضاً
فمنها ما نُقِلَ عن القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني أنَّ القدرة الحادثةَ تُؤثر في أخص وصف الفعل ؛ ككونه صلاةً أو غَصْباً أو زناً أو نحو ذلك ، لا في وجود أصل الفعل
ونُقِلَ عن الأستاذ أبي إسحاق مثلُهُ ، إِلا أَنَّهُ لَمَّا كَانَ يَقولُ بنفي الأحوالِ عبَّرَ عن أخص وصفِ الفعلِ بالوَجْهِ والاعتبارِ ، فقال : القدرة الحادثةُ تُؤثر بوجه واعتبار
ومنها ما نُقِلَ عن إمام الحرمين في آخر أمرِه : أنَّ القدرة الحادثة تُؤثر في وجودِ الفعل على وَفْق مشيئة الله تعالى
Warning
Concerning the statements of notables from Ahl al-Sunna that are not relied upon.
What we have confined ourselves to in the original treatise (aṣl al-ʿaqīda) — that created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) has absolutely no effect — is what is well-known and famous among them, which cannot be valid intellectually or legally to contradict. And some of those who are obsessed with transmitting the bad and the good of statements transmit here other statements that they also attribute to Ahl al-Sunna.
Among them is what was transmitted from al-Qāḍī Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī that the created power affects the most specific description (akhaṣṣ waṣf) of the act — such as its being prayer, usurpation, fornication, or the like — not the existence of the act itself.
And it was transmitted from al-Ustādh Abū Isḥāq the like of it, except that since he held the negation of states (aḥwāl), he expressed the most specific description of the act as "aspect and consideration" (al-wajh wa al-iʿtibār), and said: "The created power affects by way of an aspect and a consideration."
And among them is what was transmitted from Imām al-Ḥaramayn at the end of his life: that the created power affects the existence of the act in accordance with the will of God, exalted.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a warning (tanbīh) about variant opinions attributed to some Ash'ari scholars concerning the effect of created power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha). The author begins by reiterating the correct and well-known Ash'ari position: created power has absolutely no effect at all. This is the standard Ash'ari teaching, and any deviation is invalid both intellectually and legally. However, some individuals who indiscriminately transmit various statements attribute other opinions to Ahl al-Sunna. The author then lists three such opinions. First, from al-Qāḍī Abū Bakr al-Bāqillānī: created power affects the most specific description (akhaṣṣ waṣf) of an act — e.g., making it prayer, usurpation, or fornication — but not the existence of the act. Second, from al-Ustādh Abū Isḥāq al-Isfarāyīnī: a similar view, but because he rejects the theory of states (aḥwāl), he frames the specific description as 'aspect and consideration' (wajh wa iʿtibār). Third, from Imām al-Ḥaramayn al-Juwaynī in his later opinion: created power affects the existence of the act in conformity with God's will. The author implies that these opinions are not to be relied upon despite being attributed to major figures.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة (al-qudra al-ḥāditha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris believe created power has some effect.
Correction: The standard Ash'ari position is that created power has no effect at all; any effect is from Allah alone.

Checkpoint
What does the author state is the well-known position of Ahl al-Sunna regarding created power?
A) It affects the specific description of the act
B) It has no effect at all
C) It affects the existence of the act
D) It affects both existence and description

Key Takeaway
The correct Ash'ari position is that created power has no effect whatsoever; this is the only intellectually and legally valid view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you succeed in a task, do you genuinely feel that your effort was the cause, or do you see yourself as a mere channel for Allah's creation? Examine a recent success and identify where you placed the real causal power.
?
The author warns that even statements of respected scholars can be unreliable if they contradict clear truth. Is there a belief or practice you follow because of a respected figure, even though the evidence from revelation or reason goes against it? Will you surrender your heart to the truth alone?
?
If you truly believed that your ability has zero effect—that Allah alone creates every outcome—would it change how you pray, how you plan, or how you fear failure? What is one area where you can actively acknowledge Allah's sole creative power today?

Three Variant Opinions on Created Power from Ash'ari Notables
The author lists three variant opinions from Ash'ari notables that are not to be relied upon.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three variant opinions attributed to major Ash'ari scholars regarding the effect of created power, and why they are not relied upon.

Core Idea
Even great scholars had minority views, but the mainstream Ash'ari position remains clear.

While the standard Ash'ari position is that created power has no effect, some students of theology transmit other opinions from major figures. This lesson presents three such opinions — from al-Bāqillānī, al-Isfarāyīnī, and al-Juwaynī — and shows how they differ from the established teaching.

Guided Path
1
Read the author's criticism of indiscriminate transmission
Notice how the author warns against those who transmit both sound and weak statements. This sets the context for the variant opinions.
2
Examine al-Bāqillānī's opinion
Al-Bāqillānī is reported to say that created power affects the most specific description of the act, not its existence. Understand what 'specific description' means.
For example, making an act prayer or fornication.
3
Compare with al-Isfarāyīnī's similar view
Al-Isfarāyīnī holds the same view but uses different terminology (wajh wa iʿtibār) because he rejects the theory of states (aḥwāl).
This shows how theological commitments affect expression.
4
Consider al-Juwaynī's later opinion
Al-Juwaynī reportedly held that created power affects the existence of the act in accordance with God's will.
This is closer to the mainstream but still not the relied-upon view.
